<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>QUESTION AND ANSWER SECTION</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">Operator:&nbsp;&nbsp;Thank you. And at this time, we will be conducting a question-and-answer session. [Operator Instructions] Our first question comes from the line of Andrew Strelzik with BMO. Please proceed with your questions.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Andrew Strelzik &#8211; BMO Capital Markets Corp.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">All right, great. Good afternoon, everyone. Thanks for taking the question and congratulations on &#8211; certainly on the momentum that you&#8217;re seeing in the business. Where I wanted to start was trying to understand &#8211; or put in context the pricing that you&#8217;re talking about, having taken relative to the inflation that you&#8217;re expecting or that you&#8217;re seeing. So, across commodities or wages, what are you expecting for 2022 and how much does the high single-digits cover?</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Jimmy Uba &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Thank you for your question, Andrew. Before we answer your question, I would like to make a quick correction to our prepared remarks. We have nine executed leases, not seven. So, nine executed leases besides Stonestown. I just want to make sure with you guys before we answer your question.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Andrew Strelzik &#8211; BMO Capital Markets Corp.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">[indiscernible] (00:22:16).</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Jimmy Uba &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">And Steve [indiscernible] (00:22:18) question.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Sure. I&#8217;ll speak a little bit to the pricing, and Jimmy, give it over to you for further context. But just to reiterate, we made a, on average, high single-digit pricing increase move effective September 1. We took into account the competitive environment in every one of the metro areas we operate in, and we also disconnected a little bit some of our state-level pricing and looked at really on a more a market basis, where the Dallas market, let&#8217;s say, may merit or command a different pricing from Houston or Austin for instance. So, that was a change in approach for the company and also something that we think better reflects where we stand in the market. And we feel, as Jimmy noted, we&#8217;re still in a great value positioning nonetheless having taken that.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And we have been very encouraged in the first couple of months of Q1 about just how much that pricing has offset the inflationary pressures that have come primarily from food and labor. At the same time, we know there&#8217;s a lot of volatility still in both of those categories, as well as some supply chain challenges that we feel like we&#8217;re dealing with very well. But nonetheless, with the outlook still a little bit unclear as to where food and labor may go for the rest of the year, we&#8217;re not in a position yet where we&#8217;d want to get into too much detail about what we think the puts and takes are between the pricing and those costs. But we&#8217;ll say that early indications are positive. We&#8217;re pleased with how we&#8217;re getting the leveraging off of the sales with the increase that we took on September 1.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Andrew Strelzik &#8211; BMO Capital Markets Corp.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Okay. That&#8217;s helpful. And then, in the press release and the prepared remarks, there was some conversation around the efficiencies that you&#8217;re realizing. And I&#8217;m just curious if you can kind of frame where you&#8217;re seeing the biggest benefits in particular, if there&#8217;s anything new that you&#8217;ve kind of unlocked going forward. Just a little more color around what you&#8217;re doing on that side would be fantastic.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Yeah. I&#8217;ll &#8211; maybe just to speak first a little bit, I think some of what we&#8217;re looking at &#8211; and this might add on to the conversation about labor costs &#8211; is we were very &#8211; we are very pleased with how well we&#8217;ve been able to respond with staffing in our restaurants, and frankly, think we&#8217;re not experiencing the degree of shortage or challenges that maybe some others in the space have been talking about. We have virtually full operational capabilities in our restaurants right now. But at the same time, it also means that we have a number of fairly new employees to the system and we are working through, I would say, some efficiencies </font></p>
<p style="text-align:center;margin-top:12pt;margin-bottom:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">6</a></p>

<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Ben Porten &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">As Steve mentioned, the most important projects in our immediate initiative pipeline would be the table-side payment and touch panel drink ordering. We think that this will be &#8211; this will meaningfully reduce the amount of work that servers are required to do. That&#8217;s allowing us to increase our labor efficiency. In terms of margin growth, this is &#8211; we think this is our largest opportunity as well, simply because the margin growth we&#8217;ve seen in the last quarter is driven by sales leveraging. And as we can turn tables more rapidly and serve more guests per day, we think this is going to be a meaningful comp driver, especially in our mature stores.</font></p>

But I&#8217;m just curious if you think the economic model for new units that you had kind of laid out over the last couple of years, do you still think that&#8217;s the right way to think about the new unit performance or do you think maybe we&#8217;re in a better place now than we have been? And then, when the price increase went into effect, we followed that with two months of almost 19% in September and north of 20% in October. And so, we&#8217;re clearly outpacing the change in the pricing with the sequential further growth in the comps. Beyond that, the statistics around check and traffic and so forth, we&#8217;ll be in a better position at the end of the quarter to provide a more comprehensive analysis of those components. But we&#8217;re feeling very good about our customers still being there strongly no matter what, given what we&#8217;ve seen in comps since the move in price.</font></p>

<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Yeah. And so, we were running low single-digit negative in California the last couple of months of Q4. In Q1, we moved immediately to low double-digit positive in California in both September and October. And then, in Texas, we&#8217;re talking about north of 25% comp performances in each of those two months. And so, so really we&#8217;re very pleased with the trend move and just on an absolute basis, what&#8217;s happening there. And again, those are against the 2019 numbers, just to be clear, on the comps.</font></p>

<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Jeremy Hamblin &#8211; Craig-Hallum Capital Group LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Right, got it. <p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Sure. I&#8217;ll speak to &#8211; maybe it talks a little bit to the earlier question on the economic model side as well. And we&#8217;ve &#8211; throughout the pandemic and through the recovery that we&#8217;ve seen thus far, there&#8217;s nothing in it that tells us we can&#8217;t get back to the kind of pre-pandemic type restaurant economics that this business succeeded with. And if you look at the comp performance recovery and what&#8217;s happened here in the first quarter &#8211; again, I&#8217;m always going to caution that it&#8217;s early indications. But those early indications are pretty encouraging to us in terms of what we can take the business in terms of overall restaurant volumes to on a go-forward basis. With those types of numbers, it&#8217;s pretty easy to [ph] tell or see (00:34:34) that the overall restaurant volumes would be growing.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And then, also on the labor and COGS side, both areas, we thought there was strong progress sequentially where we got &#8211; on an adjusted basis, we got labor down about 200 basis points from the prior quarter to where it&#8217;s now, 34.3% of sales. COGS was 30.8% of sales. Other costs, yes, there&#8217;s inflation, but they start from a much lower base portion of our costs once you got outside of the prime area. And we considered that when we made our overall pricing move to both offset the impact of those and be able to continue leveraging restaurant economics the way we want to get to and also staying a very high value concept within our space. And so far, we feel like we&#8217;re accomplishing that.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Jeremy Hamblin &#8211; Craig-Hallum Capital Group LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Last one just...</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Ben Porten &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">And if I can just add on the off-premises that you&#8217;ve asked about, Jeremy...</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Jeremy Hamblin &#8211; Craig-Hallum Capital Group LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Yeah.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Ben Porten &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">So, typically the two incremental costs associated with growth in off-premises would be packaging costs and then delivery costs. For us, our packaging costs are basically offset because with any off-premises order, there is no disposal, whereas for in-store dining, we typically have a 3% to 4% [ph] plate (00:35:58) disposal rate. And so, that&#8217;s not a margin pressure there. And then, in terms of delivery cost, we&#8217;re &#8211; our business is almost entirely pick-up and we&#8217;re not subsidizing any of the delivery fees if a guest does opt for delivery. And so, that&#8217;s not a cost pressure either.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Jeremy Hamblin &#8211; Craig-Hallum Capital Group LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Great. Then, just one clarifying question on the menu pricing, what is your current food cost inflation rate? I think that the 30.8% in Q4 is actually the lowest food and beverage costs you&#8217;ve ever had in any quarter. And I would think maybe with the price increase that you&#8217;re probably tracking slightly below 30% food and beverage costs now.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Yeah. I&#8217;ll give a little more color on the 30.8% is that our sales mix by geography normalized a little more in the fourth quarter as well once California came fully back online with 100% indoor dining capacity. Our pricing on average is higher in California than the Texas market, for instance, because of a much different labor environment. And so, if you were to look at California restaurant P&amp;Ls overall, you&#8217;re going to see a better COGS number and you&#8217;re going to see higher labor spend. It&#8217;s just a fact of doing business here. And so, as more and more of our sales now have gotten back to California, and that&#8217;s more normal for us, that did help the move in COGS as a percent of sales.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">In terms of current rates, I&#8217;m just going to fall back again on the high-single price move that we made. We&#8217;re very pleased with how that&#8217;s helping us offset the impact of costs. And we&#8217;re also well aware that there can be shifts that happen very quickly from month to month in food. Now, we do have a very diverse menu, as you know. Our top five commodities are around only 25% combined of our total food costs. So, that diversification helps us. But when things like labor or freight, which are going to be a factor for almost all of the food that comes in, and other macro factors, it can </p>
<p style="text-align:center;margin-top:12pt;margin-bottom:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">9</a></p>

And we just feel like we&#8217;re going to have better visibility to where the food cost situation is down the road and maybe be able to give some more granularity around future expectations after that.</font></p>

Please proceed with your questions.</p>

<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Matt Curtis &#8211; William Blair &amp; Co. LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Hi. It&#8217;s Matt Curtis on for Sharon. I have a question on overall restaurant-level margins. I&#8217;m curious as to how much of a gap you think you can close in fiscal 2022.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">I&#8217;ll maybe reiterate our thoughts, but we don&#8217;t see any reason why we can&#8217;t completely recover back to the kind of restaurant-level margins that we had in the business pre-pandemic. What clouds the future maybe a little bit &#8211; or we want to hold on to and see some more experience is a little bit of the opaque nature of the cost environment in both food right now and to some degree in labor now.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And while we&#8217;re pleased with where things are going &#8211; we feel very good about the progress we made to get to the 16.4% margin in Q4 in spite of the fact that the first half of June had a very constrained California still in terms of indoor dining capacities, as well as, as I mentioned, a lot of new labor coming onboard and some learning curves and efficiency building that needs to happen with some of our newer team members. Putting that in context, we think getting to that 16.4% was a very significant and positive move, and obviously, narrowing in quickly on what our historical best was. But we&#8217;re just not at a point where we think it makes sense to try to predict specific dates or times when we get back to that historical level, but we&#8217;re very confident it&#8217;s there for us to achieve.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Matt Curtis &#8211; William Blair &amp; Co. LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">[indiscernible] (00:40:56).</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Ben Porten &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">...restaurant-level operating profit margin for the prior quarter was 5.8%. And so, the 16.4% that we saw in Q4 was tremendous growth really driven by the increased sales leveraging, and we&#8217;ve been very encouraged by the revenue that we&#8217;re seeing quarter-to-date.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>

LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Okay, understood. Thanks. <p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;"><font style="font-weight:normal;">other term structures on food. <p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And then, also from a training perspective, another area where we put some more investment at the support center line is in training programs for our team members to enhance their efficiency and customer service. And so, there&#8217;s a lot of things going on at the same time that are pointed toward we&#8217;re driving more efficiency in the business. And frankly, this is a brand that historically &#8211; when you think about the level of back-of-house robotics that have been deployed and how much this is a system based upon years of experience in Kura Japan that&#8217;s been very efficiently developed, we might not have had a whole lot of low-hanging fruit, so to speak, for efficiencies. But we&#8217;re always looking to continuously improve a number of the things I just mentioned as examples.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Matt Curtis &#8211; William Blair &amp; Co. LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Okay, got it. And then, on your G&amp;A guidance for fiscal 2022, I was hoping you could break out the components of the dollar increase in G&amp;A. It sounds like it includes technology investments and things like table-side payment and drink ordering and other things. I was wondering if you could perhaps separate that from the core G&amp;A dollar growth you&#8217;re seeing next year.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;A &#8211; Steve Benrubi &#8211; Kura Sushi USA, Inc.&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Yeah. I&#8217;ll speak to the things that really &#8211; the few pieces that if you put them together, it&#8217;s the vast majority of what is happening there, and it does start with people. When it comes to the leadership side of the business, in addition to Sean coming on as COO, Arlene, our Chief People Officer, joined the company just recently. And we also brought onboard a Director of IT, whereas that function &#8211; we have managed it historically through almost all of our support coming from third-party service organizations. And we&#8217;ve reached a scale where we believe it&#8217;s time that we build our own IT skill set in-house. And so, we hired that and have intention to bring on a couple of staff members to help support IT under that director as well.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And then, there have been some investments that were made late in fiscal 2021 in people that have already been showing signs of paying strong dividends for us. And that&#8217;s in the recruiting area, where we brought on a few more team members for restaurant-level recruiting, and also in the store opening area, where we brought on a whole additional store opening team. Because when we get to the point now where we&#8217;re talking about opening 8 to 10 restaurants, we really need two teams working concurrently there. And you saw the benefit of those additions in how well we&#8217;ve been able to staff our restaurants. From the June 15 so-called reopening of California when it got to 100% up to now, the kinds of sales recovery and comp store sales we&#8217;re talking about through October simply couldn&#8217;t have happened without us having a strong staffing level at almost all of our restaurants. And those recruiting folks and those opening team people have been tremendously contributive to making that happen.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-weight:normal;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">And then, when you put alongside some of the people costs, there&#8217;s things like travel that go along with that, getting out to the restaurants again when during the COVID area, there&#8217;s just frankly wasn&#8217;t nearly as much of that happening. There&#8217;s some things that come along with our scale of growth like insurance costs, D&amp;O and other programs, where some of those costs increased as well. And then, also as we&#8217;ve hired on people in the organization to provide support for a more aggressive growth plan, recognizing we&#8217;re now a bigger business, the span of responsibility in some positions becomes a bigger thing. And so, the hiring rates you have to bring people on can be different from what you may have been when the company was half this current size. So, I think those &#8211; if you put those elements together, that pretty much comprises the lion&#8217;s share of what&#8217;s changing in G&amp;A, and we&#8217;re just getting ahead of supporting our business, so that we make sure we grow smart.</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-weight:bold;font-family:Arial;font-size:10pt;font-style:normal;text-transform:none;font-variant: normal;">&lt;Q &#8211; Matt Curtis &#8211; William Blair &amp; Co. LLC&gt;: <font style="font-weight:normal;">Okay. So, I guess would it be...</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>

And so, really all that the employees need to do is just grab the clean plates, and it&#8217;s not something you ever need to think about again.</font></p>
<p style="margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-indent:0%;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;">&nbsp;</p>

And so, we&#8217;re particularly excited about that one. But looking at the near-term, the table-side payment and the touch panel drink ordering are the ones that are closest to full rollout.</p>
